type=&quot;video/webm; codecs=&amp;quot;vp8, vorbis&amp;quot;&quot; data-title=&quot;Small WebM (240P)&quot; data-shorttitle=&quot;WebM 240P&quot; data-transcodekey=&quot;240p.webm&quot; data-width=&quot;320&quot; data-height=&quot;240&quot; data-bandwidth=&quot;324840&quot; data-framerate=&quot;25&quot;/&gt;&lt;/video&gt;&lt;/div&gt;"><img alt="File:Burning Magnesium Block!.ogv" style="width:220px;height:165px" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Burning_Magnesium_Block%21.ogv/220px--Burning_Magnesium_Block%21.ogv.jpg" /><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/db/Burning_Magnesium_Block%21.ogv" title="Play media" target="new"><span class="play-btn-large"><span class="mw-tmh-playtext">Play media</span></span></a></div>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Burning_Magnesium_Block!.ogv" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Magnesium block heated with <a href="/wiki/Blow_torch" class="mw-redirect" title="Blow torch">blowtorch</a> to self-combustion, emitting intense white light</div></div></div>
<p>Magnesium metal and its alloys can be explosive hazards; they are highly flammable in their pure form when molten or in powder or ribbon form. Burning or molten magnesium reacts violently with water. When working with powdered magnesium, <a href="/wiki/Safety_glasses" class="mw-redirect" title="Safety glasses">safety glasses</a> with <a href="/wiki/Eye_protection" title="Eye protection">eye protection</a> and UV filters (such as welders use) are employed because burning magnesium produces <a href="/wiki/Ultraviolet" title="Ultraviolet">ultraviolet</a> light that can permanently damage the <a href="/wiki/Retina" title="Retina">retina</a> of a human eye.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Magnesium is capable of reducing <a href="/wiki/Water_(molecule)" class="mw-redirect" title="Water (molecule)">water</a> and releasing highly flammable <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen" title="Hydrogen">hydrogen</a> gas:<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dd>Mg (s) + 2 <span class="chemf nowrap">H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br /><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>O</span> (l) → <a href="/wiki/Magnesium_hydroxide" title="Magnesium hydroxide"><span class="chemf nowrap">Mg(OH)<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br /><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span></a> (s) + <span class="chemf nowrap">H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br /><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span> (g)</dd></dl>
<p>Therefore, water cannot extinguish magnesium fires. The hydrogen gas produced intensifies the fire. Dry sand is an effective smothering agent, but only on relatively level and flat surfaces.
</p><p>Magnesium reacts with <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a> exothermically to form <a href="/wiki/Magnesium_oxide" title="Magnesium oxide">magnesium oxide</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carbon" title="Carbon">carbon</a>:<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dd>2 Mg + <span class="chemf nowrap">CO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br /><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span> → 2 MgO + C (s)</dd></dl>
<p>Hence, carbon dioxide fuels rather than extinguishes magnesium fires.
</p><p>Burning magnesium can be quenched by using a <a href="/wiki/Fire_extinguisher#Class_D" title="Fire extinguisher">Class D</a> dry chemical fire extinguisher, or by covering the fire with <a href="/wiki/Sand" title="Sand">sand</a> or magnesium foundry flux to remove its air source.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Useful_compounds">Useful compounds</span></h2>
<p>Magnesium compounds, primarily <a href="/wiki/Magnesium_oxide" title="Magnesium oxide">magnesium oxide</a> (MgO), are used as a <a href="/wiki/Refractory" title="Refractory">refractory</a> material in <a href="/wiki/Furnace" title="Furnace">furnace</a> linings for producing <a href="/wiki/Iron" title="Iron">iron</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steel" title="Steel">steel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nonferrous_metal" class="mw-redirect" title="Nonferrous metal">nonferrous metals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glass" title="Glass">glass</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cement" title="Cement">cement</a>.  Magnesium oxide and other magnesium compounds are also used in the agricultural, chemical, and construction industries. Magnesium oxide from <a href="/wiki/Calcination" title="Calcination">calcination</a> is used as an electrical insulator in <a href="/wiki/Mineral-insulated_copper-clad_cable" title="Mineral-insulated copper-clad cable">fire-resistant cables</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Magnesium reacted with an <a href="/wiki/Alkyl_halide" class="mw-redirect" title="Alkyl halide">alkyl halide</a> gives a <a href="/wiki/Grignard_reaction" title="Grignard reaction">Grignard reagent</a>, which is a very useful tool for preparing <a href="/wiki/Alcohols" class="mw-redirect" title="Alcohols">alcohols</a>.
</p><p>Magnesium salts are included in various <a href="/wiki/Food" title="Food">foods</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fertilizer" title="Fertilizer">fertilizers</a> (magnesium is a component of <a href="/wiki/Chlorophyll" title="Chlorophyll">chlorophyll</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Culture_medium" class="mw-redirect" title="Culture medium">microbe culture media</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Magnesium_sulfite" title="Magnesium sulfite">Magnesium sulfite</a> is used in the manufacture of <a href="/wiki/Paper" title="Paper">paper</a> (<a href="/wiki/Sulfite_process" title="Sulfite process">sulfite process</a>).
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Magnesium_phosphate" title="Magnesium phosphate">Magnesium phosphate</a> is used to fireproof wood used in construction.
</p><p>Magnesium hexafluorosilicate is used for moth-proofing <a href="/wiki/Textile" title="Textile">textiles</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Biological_roles">Biological roles</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Magnesium_in_biology" title="Magnesium in biology">Magnesium in biology</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mechanism_of_action">Mechanism of action</span></h3>
<p>The important interaction between <a href="/wiki/Phosphate" title="Phosphate">phosphate</a> and magnesium ions makes magnesium essential to the basic <a href="/wiki/Nucleic_acid" title="Nucleic acid">nucleic acid</a> chemistry of all cells of all known living organisms. More than 300 <a href="/wiki/Enzyme" title="Enzyme">enzymes</a> require magnesium ions for their catalytic action, including all enzymes using or synthesizing <a href="/wiki/Adenosine_triphosphate" title="Adenosine triphosphate">ATP</a> and those that use other <a href="/wiki/Nucleotides" class="mw-redirect" title="Nucleotides">nucleotides</a> to synthesize <a href="/wiki/DNA" title="DNA">DNA</a> and <a href="/wiki/RNA" title="RNA">RNA</a>. The ATP molecule is normally found in a <a href="/wiki/Chelation" title="Chelation">chelate</a> with a magnesium ion.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Dietary_sources.2C_recommended_intake.2C_and_supplementation"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Dietary_sources,_recommended_intake,_and_supplementation">Dietary sources, recommended intake, and supplementation</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FoodSourcesOfMagnesium.jpg" class="image"><img alt="refer to caption; follow link for complete description" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/FoodSourcesOfMagnesium.jpg/170px-FoodSourcesOfMagnesium.jpg" width="170" height="261" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/FoodSourcesOfMagnesium.jpg/255px-FoodSourcesOfMagnesium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/FoodSourcesOfMagnesium.jpg/340px-FoodSourcesOfMagnesium.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1759" data-file-height="2700" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FoodSourcesOfMagnesium.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Examples of food sources of magnesium  (clockwise from top left): bran muffins, pumpkin seeds, barley, buckwheat flour, low-fat vanilla yogurt, trail mix, halibut steaks, garbanzo beans, lima beans, soybeans, and spinach</div></div></div><p> Spices, nuts, cereals, cocoa and vegetables are rich sources of magnesium.<sup id="cite_ref-nih_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nih-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Green leafy vegetables such as <a href="/wiki/Spinach" title="Spinach">spinach</a> are also rich in magnesium.<sup id="cite_ref-mlp_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mlp-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">UK</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Dietary_Reference_Intake" title="Dietary Reference Intake">recommended daily values</a> for magnesium are 300&#160;mg for men and 270&#160;mg for women.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> In the U.S. the Recommended Dietary Allowances (RDAs) are 400&#160;mg for men ages 19–30 and 420&#160;mg for older; for women 310&#160;mg for ages 19–30 and 320&#160;mg for older.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Numerous <a href="/wiki/Magnesium_(pharmaceutical_preparation)" class="mw-redirect" title="Magnesium (pharmaceutical preparation)">pharmaceutical preparations of magnesium</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dietary_supplement" title="Dietary supplement">dietary supplements</a> are available. In two human trials magnesium oxide, one of the most common forms in magnesium dietary supplements because of its high magnesium content per weight, was less bioavailable than magnesium citrate, chloride, lactate or aspartate.<sup id="cite_ref-Firoz2001_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Firoz2001-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lindberg1990_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lindberg1990-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Metabolism">Metabolism</span></h3>
<p>An adult has 22–26&#160;grams of magnesium,<sup id="cite_ref-nih_8-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nih-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> with 60% in the <a href="/wiki/Skeleton" title="Skeleton">skeleton</a>, 39% intracellular (20% in skeletal muscle), and 1% extracellular.<sup id="cite_ref-nih_8-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nih-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Serum levels are typically 0.7–1.0&#160;mmol/L or 1.8–2.4 mEq/L. Serum magnesium levels may be normal even when intracellular magnesium is deficient. The mechanisms for maintaining the magnesium level in the serum are varying <a href="/wiki/Gastrointestinal_tract" title="Gastrointestinal tract">gastrointestinal</a> absorption and <a href="/wiki/Renal" class="mw-redirect" title="Renal">renal</a> excretion. Intracellular magnesium is correlated with intracellular <a href="/wiki/Potassium" title="Potassium">potassium</a>. Increased magnesium lowers <a href="/wiki/Calcium" title="Calcium">calcium</a><sup id="cite_ref-ummedu_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ummedu-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> and can either prevent hypercalcemia or cause hypocalcemia depending on the initial level.<sup id="cite_ref-ummedu_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ummedu-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Both low and high protein intake conditions inhibit magnesium absorption, as does the amount of <a href="/wiki/Phosphate" title="Phosphate">phosphate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phytate" class="mw-redirect" title="Phytate">phytate</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fat" title="Fat">fat</a> in the gut. Unabsorbed dietary magnesium is excreted in feces; absorbed magnesium is excreted in urine and sweat.<sup id="cite_ref-Wester1987_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wester1987-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Detection_in_serum_and_plasma">Detection in serum and plasma</span></h3>
<p>Magnesium status may be assessed by measuring serum and erythrocyte magnesium concentrations coupled with <a href="/wiki/Urinary_system" title="Urinary system">urinary</a> and <a href="/wiki/Feces" title="Feces">fecal</a> magnesium content, but intravenous magnesium loading tests are more accurate and practical.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> A retention of 20% or more of the injected amount indicates deficiency.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> No <a href="/wiki/Biomarker" title="Biomarker">biomarker</a> has been established for magnesium.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Magnesium concentrations in plasma or serum may be monitored for efficacy and safety in those receiving the drug <a href="/wiki/Therapy" title="Therapy">therapeutically</a>, to confirm the diagnosis in potential <a href="/wiki/Poison" title="Poison">poisoning</a> victims, or to assist in the <a href="/wiki/Forensic_science" title="Forensic science">forensic</a> investigation in a case of fatal overdose. The newborn children of mothers who received <a href="/wiki/Parenteral_nutrition" title="Parenteral nutrition">parenteral</a> magnesium sulfate during labor may exhibit toxicity with normal serum magnesium levels.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Deficiency">Deficiency</span></h3>
<p>Low plasma magnesium (<a href="/wiki/Hypomagnesemia" class="mw-redirect" title="Hypomagnesemia">hypomagnesemia</a>) is common: it is found in 2.5–15% of the general population.<sup id="cite_ref-Ayuk_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ayuk-57">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> From 2005 to 2006, 48 percent of the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> population consumed less magnesium than recommended in the <a href="/wiki/Dietary_Reference_Intake" title="Dietary Reference Intake">Dietary Reference Intake</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Other causes are increased renal or gastrointestinal loss, an increased intracellular shift, and proton-pump inhibitor antacid therapy. Most are asymptomatic, but symptoms referable to <a href="/wiki/Neuromuscular_medicine" title="Neuromuscular medicine">neuromuscular</a>, <a href="/wiki/Circulatory_system" title="Circulatory system">cardiovascular</a>, and metabolic dysfunction may occur.<sup id="cite_ref-Ayuk_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ayuk-57">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alcoholism" title="Alcoholism">Alcoholism</a> is often associated with magnesium deficiency. Chronically low serum magnesium levels are associated with <a href="/wiki/Metabolic_syndrome" title="Metabolic syndrome">metabolic syndrome</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diabetes_mellitus_type_2" title="Diabetes mellitus type 2">diabetes mellitus type 2</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fasciculation" title="Fasciculation">fasciculation</a>, and hypertension.<sup id="cite_ref-Geiger2012_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Geiger2012-59">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Therapy">Therapy</span></h3>
<ul><li>Intravenous magnesium is recommended by the ACC/AHA/ESC 2006 Guidelines for Management of Patients With Ventricular Arrhythmias and the Prevention of Sudden Cardiac Death for patients with ventricular <a href="/wiki/Heart_arrhythmia" title="Heart arrhythmia">arrhythmia</a> associated with <a href="/wiki/Torsades_de_pointes" title="Torsades de pointes">torsades de pointes</a> who present with <a href="/wiki/Long_QT_syndrome" title="Long QT syndrome">long QT syndrome</a>; and for the treatment of patients with digoxin induced arrhythmias.<sup id="cite_ref-Zipes2006_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zipes2006-60">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Magnesium sulfate – intravenous – is used for the management of <a href="/wiki/Pre-eclampsia" title="Pre-eclampsia">pre-eclampsia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eclampsia" title="Eclampsia">eclampsia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-James2010_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-James2010-61">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Euser2009_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Euser2009-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Hypomagnesemia, including that caused by alcoholism, is reversible by oral or parenteral magnesium administration depending on the degree of deficiency.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>There is limited evidence that magnesium supplementation may play a role in the prevention and treatment of <a href="/wiki/Migraine" title="Migraine">migraine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-migraine_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-migraine-64">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Sorted by type of magnesium salt, other therapeutic applications include:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Magnesium_sulfate" title="Magnesium sulfate">Magnesium sulfate</a>, as the <a href="/wiki/Hydrate" title="Hydrate">heptahydrate</a> called Epsom salts, is used as <a href="/wiki/Bath_salts" title="Bath salts">bath salts</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Laxative" title="Laxative">laxative</a>, and a highly soluble <a href="/wiki/Fertilizer" title="Fertilizer">fertilizer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Magnesium_hydroxide" title="Magnesium hydroxide">Magnesium hydroxide</a>, suspended in water, is used in <a href="/wiki/Milk_of_magnesia" class="mw-redirect" title="Milk of magnesia">milk of magnesia</a> <a href="/wiki/Antacid" title="Antacid">antacids</a> and <a href="/wiki/Laxative" title="Laxative">laxatives</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Magnesium_chloride" title="Magnesium chloride">Magnesium chloride</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magnesium_oxide" title="Magnesium oxide">oxide</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magnesium_gluconate" title="Magnesium gluconate">gluconate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magnesium_malate" title="Magnesium malate">malate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magnesium_orotate" title="Magnesium orotate">orotate</a>, glycinate, <a href="/wiki/Ascorbate" class="mw-redirect" title="Ascorbate">ascorbate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Magnesium_citrate" title="Magnesium citrate">citrate</a> are all used as oral magnesium supplements.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Borate" title="Borate">Magnesium borate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magnesium_salicylate" title="Magnesium salicylate">magnesium salicylate</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Magnesium_sulfate" title="Magnesium sulfate">magnesium sulfate</a> are used as <a href="/wiki/Antiseptic" title="Antiseptic">antiseptics</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Magnesium_bromide" title="Magnesium bromide">Magnesium bromide</a> is used as a mild <a href="/wiki/Sedative" title="Sedative">sedative</a> (this action is due to the <a href="/wiki/Bromide" title="Bromide">bromide</a>, not the magnesium).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Magnesium_stearate" title="Magnesium stearate">Magnesium stearate</a> is a slightly <a href="/wiki/Fire" title="Fire">flammable</a> white <a href="/wiki/Powder_(substance)" class="mw-redirect" title="Powder (substance)">powder</a> with <a href="/wiki/Lubricant" title="Lubricant">lubricating</a> properties. In <a href="/wiki/Pharmacology" title="Pharmacology">pharmaceutical</a> technology, it is used in pharmacological manufacture to prevent <a href="/wiki/Tablet_(pharmacy)" title="Tablet (pharmacy)">tablets</a> from sticking to the equipment while compressing the ingredients into tablet form.</li>
<li>Magnesium carbonate powder is used by athletes such as <a href="/wiki/Gymnastics" title="Gymnastics">gymnasts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Olympic_weightlifting" title="Olympic weightlifting">weightlifters</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Climbing" title="Climbing">climbers</a> to eliminate palm sweat, prevent sticking, and improve the grip on gymnastic apparatus, lifting bars, and climbing rocks.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overdose">Overdose</span></h3>
<p>Overdose from dietary sources alone is unlikely because excess magnesium in the blood is promptly filtered by the <a href="/wiki/Kidney" title="Kidney">kidneys</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Ayuk_57-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ayuk-57">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> and overdose is more likely in the presence of impaired renal function. In spite of this, <a href="/wiki/Megavitamin_therapy" title="Megavitamin therapy">megadose therapy</a> has caused death in a young child,<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> and severe <a href="/wiki/Hypermagnesemia" title="Hypermagnesemia">hypermagnesemia</a> in a woman<sup id="cite_ref-Kontani_M,_Hara_A,_Ohta_S,_Ikeda_T_2005_448–452_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kontani_M,_Hara_A,_Ohta_S,_Ikeda_T_2005_448–452-67">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> and a young girl<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> who had healthy kidneys.
The most common symptoms of overdose are <a href="/wiki/Nausea" title="Nausea">nausea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vomiting" title="Vomiting">vomiting</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Diarrhea" title="Diarrhea">diarrhea</a>; other symptoms include <a href="/wiki/Hypotension" title="Hypotension">hypotension</a>, confusion, slowed heart and <a href="/wiki/Respiratory_system" title="Respiratory system">respiratory</a> rate, deficiencies of other minerals, <a href="/wiki/Coma" title="Coma">coma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cardiac_arrhythmia/bradycardia" class="mw-redirect" title="Cardiac arrhythmia/bradycardia">cardiac arrhythmia</a>, and death from <a href="/wiki/Cardiac_arrest" title="Cardiac arrest">cardiac arrest</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ummedu_51-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ummedu-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Function_in_plants">Function in plants</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Plants" class="mw-redirect" title="Plants">Plants</a> require magnesium to synthesize <a href="/wiki/Chlorophyll" title="Chlorophyll">chlorophyll</a>, essential for <a href="/wiki/Photosynthesis" title="Photosynthesis">photosynthesis</a>. Magnesium in the center of the <a href="/wiki/Porphyrin_ring" class="mw-redirect" title="Porphyrin ring">porphyrin ring</a> in chlorophyll functions in a manner similar to the iron in the center of the porphyrin ring in <a href="/wiki/Heme" title="Heme">heme</a>. <a href="/wiki/Magnesium_deficiency_(plants)" class="mw-redirect" title="Magnesium deficiency (plants)">Magnesium deficiency</a> in plants causes late-season yellowing between leaf veins, especially in older leaves, and can be corrected by either applying <a href="/wiki/Epsom_salts" class="mw-redirect" title="Epsom salts">epsom salts</a> (which is rapidly <a href="/wiki/Leaching_(chemical_science)" class="mw-redirect" title="Leaching (chemical science)">leached</a>), or crushed <a href="/wiki/Dolomite" title="Dolomite">dolomitic</a> <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a>, to the soil.
</p>

"An evidence-based review of oral magnesium supplementation in the preventive treatment of migraine". <i>Cephalalgia</i> (Review). <b>35</b> (10): 912–922. <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">doi</a>:<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//doi.org/10.1177%2F0333102414564891">10.1177/0333102414564891</a>. <a href="/wiki/PubMed_Identifier" class="mw-redirect" title="PubMed Identifier">PMID</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/25533715">25533715</a>. <q>There is a strong body of evidence demonstrating a relationship between magnesium status and migraine. Magnesium likely plays a role in migraine development at a biochemical level, but the role of oral magnesium supplementation in migraine prophylaxis and treatment remains to be fully elucidated. The strength of evidence supporting oral magnesium supplementation is limited at this time.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Cephalalgia&amp;rft.atitle=An+evidence-based+review+of+oral+magnesium+supplementation+in+the+preventive+treatment+of+migraine&amp;rft.volume=35&amp;rft.issue=10&amp;rft.pages=912-922&amp;rft.date=2014&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1177%2F0333102414564891&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F25533715&amp;rft.aulast=Teigen&amp;rft.aufirst=L&amp;rft.au=Boes%2C+CJ&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMagnesium" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-65"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-65">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Gowariker, Vasant; Krishnamurthy, V.
